#### What this PR does / why we need it:
The feature aims to improve performance and practicality by reducing the overhead of distributing workloads to all clusters simultaneously, minimizing the risk of duplicate admissions and unnecessary preemptions. 
It should  prevent triggering autoscaling across multiple worker clusters at the same time.


#### Which issue(s) this PR fixes:
<!--
*Automatically closes linked issue when PR is merged.
Usage: `Fixes #<issue number>`, or `Fixes (paste link of issue)`.
_If PR is about `failing-tests or flakes`, please post the related issues/tests in a comment and do not use `Fixes`_*
-->
Fixes #5141

### Comment by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) — 2025-05-29T07:52:41Z

Ww need to discuss also the granularity of the timeout as mentioned by @mimowo 

> should the timeout be global, per manager, or per worker

### Comment by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) — 2025-05-29T08:01:44Z

In my opinion this is not if, but how we deliver those levels for timeout, because we already see at leat 2 scenarios that require different levels.
One was mentioned in #5141 and the other in #3757.

This is one could be more general, timeout for the similar type of large amount of clusters.
> Both performance (distributing and keeping 40 copies of workload in cluster informers can be expensive) and practical (trying all 40 clusters at the very same time can lead to lots of unnecessary preemptions).

This one should be more granular, probably on the worker level, different clusters but not many of them.
> To prioritize the use of some clusters over others. For example a user may have one cluster with reservations, and one auto-scaled. The user prefers to first try the reservation cluster, and only as a fallback try autoscaling.

## Reviews

### Review by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) (commented) — 2025-05-29T10:41:21Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:311** by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) — 2025-05-29T10:41:21Z
```diff
@@ -304,6 +303,19 @@ type MultiKueue struct {
 	GCInterval *metav1.Duration `json:"gcInterval"`
 	Origin *string `json:"origin,omitempty"`
 	WorkerLostTimeout *metav1.Duration `json:"workerLostTimeout,omitempty"`
+  Dispatcher *MultiKueueWorkloadDispatcher `json:"multiKueueWorkloadDispatcher,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueWorkloadDispatcher struct {
+  // Strategy defines the strategy for selecting a worker cluster to handle the workload.
+  // - All: The initial MultiKueue behavior where the workload is distributed to all workers simultaneously,
```

  This is added on purpose, maybe we want to keep the old behaviour for some users. wdyt?

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-05-29T11:05:23Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:314** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-05-29T11:05:23Z
```diff
@@ -304,6 +303,19 @@ type MultiKueue struct {
 	GCInterval *metav1.Duration `json:"gcInterval"`
 	Origin *string `json:"origin,omitempty"`
 	WorkerLostTimeout *metav1.Duration `json:"workerLostTimeout,omitempty"`
+  Dispatcher *MultiKueueWorkloadDispatcher `json:"multiKueueWorkloadDispatcher,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueWorkloadDispatcher struct {
+  // Strategy defines the strategy for selecting a worker cluster to handle the workload.
+  // - All: The initial MultiKueue behavior where the workload is distributed to all workers simultaneously,
+  //        and the first worker to successfully reserve the workload's required resources is selected.
+  // - RoundRobin: Distributes the workload to one worker at a time in a circular order.
+  Strategy MultiKueueWorkloadDispatcherStrategy `json:"strategy"`
```

  Maybe MultiKueueWorkloadDispatcherStrategy should be enum corresponding to two strategies:
  - TryAllAtOnce
  - Dispatcher
  
  When the Dispatcher is set, then MultiKueue would wait for the Dispatcher to set the value of the new API field "status.multiKueueNominatedCluster=w2". After the timeout passes it should wait for the new nominated cluster to be set by the dispatcher. This way the dispatcher could be a plugin which does prioritization and round-robin of the clusters. 
  
  Another possibility is that the dispatcher sets `status.multiKueueClustersOrder=[w2,w3,w1]`  and Kueue sequentially probes them in the specified order. This model is probably simpler to implement.
  
  Then we need to have some `spec.dispatcher` field to indicate if this is a custom dispatcher of built-in. For example it could be string similar to provisioningClassName in ProvisioningRequest.
  
  For now this is just a high level overview, I think this is a challenging problem which requires more API design.
  cc @tenzen-y @mwielgus

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2025-06-12T21:55:30Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:246** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2025-06-12T21:55:30Z
```diff
@@ -231,11 +232,42 @@ has a valid configuration and at least one of its MultiKueueClusters is `Active`
 Will monitor the workloads in the management cluster and manage their MultiKueue specific
 AdmissionCheckStates.
 
-When distributing the workloads across clusters MultiKueue Workloads controller will first create
-the Kueue's internal Workload object. Only after the workload is admitted and other clusters
-are cleaned-up the real job will be created, to match the Workload. That gives the guarantee
-that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
-get the annotation stating where it is actually running.
+When distributing workloads across clusters, the MultiKueue Workload Controller follows a two-phase
+process for a set of worker clusters selection.
+
+##### Cluster Nomination Phase
+The process of selecting a worker cluster for a workload depends on the dispatching mode configured
+for the Dispatcher. MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: Built-in, Sequential, External.
+
+* Built-in Mode:
+In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching, workload is copied to each worker
+cluster.
+
+* Sequential Mode:
```

  I don't understand this mode. Why only one cluster is selected? Based on what criterias?

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2025-06-12T21:57:11Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:255** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2025-06-12T21:57:11Z
```diff
@@ -231,11 +232,42 @@ has a valid configuration and at least one of its MultiKueueClusters is `Active`
 Will monitor the workloads in the management cluster and manage their MultiKueue specific
 AdmissionCheckStates.
 
-When distributing the workloads across clusters MultiKueue Workloads controller will first create
-the Kueue's internal Workload object. Only after the workload is admitted and other clusters
-are cleaned-up the real job will be created, to match the Workload. That gives the guarantee
-that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
-get the annotation stating where it is actually running.
+When distributing workloads across clusters, the MultiKueue Workload Controller follows a two-phase
+process for a set of worker clusters selection.
+
+##### Cluster Nomination Phase
+The process of selecting a worker cluster for a workload depends on the dispatching mode configured
+for the Dispatcher. MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: Built-in, Sequential, External.
+
+* Built-in Mode:
+In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching, workload is copied to each worker
+cluster.
+
+* Sequential Mode:
+In this mode, only one cluster is chosen at a time for dispatching. The MultiKueue Workload Controller
+nominates a single cluster by setting the `.status.multiKueueNominatedCluster` field. 
+
+* External Mode:
+In this mode, the selection of the worker cluster is entirely delegated to an external controller. The
+external controller is responsible for setting the `.status.multiKueueNominatedCluster` field to the name of
+the selected clusters.
+
+Kueue controls the time window `.disaptcher.RoundTimeout` during which the nominated clusters have the opportunity 
```

  What happens after roundTimeout?

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2025-06-12T22:00:38Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:341** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2025-06-12T22:00:37Z
```diff
@@ -304,6 +336,23 @@ type MultiKueue struct {
 	GCInterval *metav1.Duration `json:"gcInterval"`
 	Origin *string `json:"origin,omitempty"`
 	WorkerLostTimeout *metav1.Duration `json:"workerLostTimeout,omitempty"`
+  Dispatcher *MultiKueueWorkloadDispatcher `json:"multiKueueWorkloadDispatcher,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const(
+  DispatcherModeBuiltIn = "BuiltIn"
+  DispatcherModeSequential = "Sequential"
+)
+
+type MultiKueueWorkloadDispatcher struct {
+// DispatcherName defines the dispatcher responsible for selecting worker clusters to handle the workload.
+// - If specified, the workload will be handled by the named dispatcher.
+// - If not specified, the workload will be handled by the default (BuiltIn) dispatcher.
+  DispatcherName *string `json:"dispatcherName,omitempty"`
+
+// RoundTimeout specifies the duration given to a selected workers to attempt to reserve the workload's required resources.
+// This field is only applicable when the DispatcherName is specified. Defaults to 5 min.
+  RoundTimeout *metav1.Duration `json:"timeout,omitempty"`
```

  This is specific to Sequential dispatcher and should probably go to sequential dispatcher configuration.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-06-13T07:31:17Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:337** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-06-13T07:31:17Z
```diff
@@ -304,6 +336,23 @@ type MultiKueue struct {

+
+const(
+  DispatcherModeBuiltIn = "BuiltIn"
+  DispatcherModeSequential = "Sequential"

+
+type MultiKueueWorkloadDispatcher struct {
+// DispatcherName defines the dispatcher responsible for selecting worker clusters to handle the workload.
+// - If specified, the workload will be handled by the named dispatcher.
+// - If not specified, the workload will be handled by the default (BuiltIn) dispatcher.
+  DispatcherName *string `json:"dispatcherName,omitempty"`
```

  For pluggable APIs use the domain prefix to indicate the plugin provider. 
  
  For example look at definition of Job [ManagedBY API](https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/blob/8458cfed43f96e05fac0bfa43fbec473c39d5689/pkg/apis/batch/types.go#L462-L470), example value being `kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue`.
  
  Maybe:  `kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once` and `kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-sequential` (but we can discuss particular names in other comments)

+When distributing workloads across clusters, the MultiKueue Workload Controller follows a two-phase
+process for a set of worker clusters selection.
+
+##### Cluster Nomination Phase
+The process of selecting a worker cluster for a workload depends on the dispatching mode configured
+for the Dispatcher. MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: Built-in, Sequential, External.
+
+* Built-in Mode:
+In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching, workload is copied to each worker
+cluster.
+
+* Sequential Mode:

+nominates a single cluster by setting the `.status.multiKueueNominatedCluster` field.

+external controller is responsible for setting the `.status.multiKueueNominatedCluster` field to the name of
+the selected clusters.

```

  I can ad more description here, e.g:
  ```
  If the cluster fails to admit the workload within
  the allocated time, Kueue unlocks the possibility for the external controller (in External Mode) to set a new value for
  `.status.multiKueueNominatedCluster`, allowing other clusters to be nominated.
  ```

### Review by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) (commented) — 2025-06-20T12:02:34Z

+When distributing workloads across clusters, the MultiKueue Workload Controller follows a two-phase
+process for a set of worker clusters selection.
+##### Cluster Nomination Phase
+The process of selecting worker clusters for a workload depends on the dispatching mode configured
+for the Dispatcher. MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllClusters (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllClusters Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds. In each round, a new cluster is added to the set of previously nominated clusters by updating the `.status.multiKueueNominatedCluster` field to include the new cluster. This allows the workload to be considered by an increasing set of clusters over time, rather than all at once.
```

  As we synced with @mszadkow, please move  `status.multiKueueNominatedCluster` into spec. 
  
  Please also describe the API as in the following style https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/tree/main/keps/2724-topology-aware-scheduling#admin-facing-api

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-06-27T06:12:44Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:338** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-06-27T06:12:44Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,71 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo

 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller follows a two-step process: first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination Phase
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllClusters (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllClusters Mode**:  
```

  Let's align the naming consistently, either:
  - AllAtOnce
  - AllClusters
  - AllWorkers
  I'm good with any of them, maybe slightly leaning to AllAtOnce, but most importantly we should align them

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-06-27T10:23:11Z

+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-06-27T10:23:39Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:359** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-06-27T10:23:39Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,72 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller follows a two-step process: first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination Phase
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+  The workload's status condition `HaveNominatedWorkers` stores the round duration starting time.
+  This allows the controller to determine when to advance to the next nomination round based on the elapsed time since the round began.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated,
+  even if they were previously admitted there.
+
+
+#### Workload Synchronization Phase
```

  ```suggestion
  #### Workload Synchronization
  ```
  As mentioned in other comments

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-06-27T10:32:56Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:375** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-06-27T10:32:48Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,72 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller follows a two-step process: first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination Phase
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+  The workload's status condition `HaveNominatedWorkers` stores the round duration starting time.
+  This allows the controller to determine when to advance to the next nomination round based on the elapsed time since the round began.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated,
+  even if they were previously admitted there.
+
+
+#### Workload Synchronization Phase
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+
+// MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+// This field is optional.
+MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  I would like to make it immutable while the workload is admitted.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-06-27T13:24:06Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:356** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-06-27T13:24:06Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,72 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller follows a two-step process: first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination Phase
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+  The workload's status condition `HaveNominatedWorkers` stores the round duration starting time.
+  This allows the controller to determine when to advance to the next nomination round based on the elapsed time since the round began.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated,
+  even if they were previously admitted there.
```

  I would suggest to make it immutable once the workload is admitted. There is a small race condition if someone wants to modify the multiKueueNominatedClusters, and we don't yet see the event that the workload is admitted. In this case, indeed, we may update the nominated clusters, but I would make it as a note, or even leave to implementation decisions. What is important is to make it immutable once we realize the workload is admitted.

```

  Actually, I think for the simplicity of the implementation we can assume the time is measured just "in-memory", because in case of Kueue restart we will just spend additional 5min in the same round, this is acceptable I think. We can leave it as a potential improvement based on user feedback.
  
  You can mention the condition in the alternatives.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-06-27T17:53:18Z

Importantly we should also add a user story for introducing the dispatcher API, and sequential dispatcher.

Say "Story 3"

As a user of MultiKueue I would like to have a control over the dispatching of workloads to the worker clusters. In particular:
a) I would like to be able to use my custom dispatching algorithm which can prioritize the order of clusters according to some in-house information
b) I would like to use a built-in dispatching algorithm which adds clusters incrementally, rather than trying all of them at once. This is important to avoid preemptions happening in all clusters at the same time during the admission.

+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  If this field will be set by kueue-controller-manager, I this this should be status field.
  Because basically, kueue-controller-manager should not have permission to operate the reconciliation object spec.
  
  This is the same problem as the active field.

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:337** by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2025-06-27T18:04:27Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,76 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
```

  Is this `kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once` dispatcher name?
  If yes, is this specified in the dispatcherName field in MultiKueue?

+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+

+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.

+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.

@@ -316,6 +323,76 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
```

  ```suggestion
    While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is immutable. 
  ```
  The sentence below is just repeating what immutable means.

 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.

+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
```

  ```suggestion
    // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted' && c.status == "True")) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
  ```

+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
```

  When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
  the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
  specified in the Workload's `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field. 
  
  While the Workload is pending, the dispatcher can add or remove clusters from the list, and the Workload
  Controller synchronizes the value of the field with the subset of worker clusters with the Workload copy.

```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,76 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
```

  ```suggestion
    The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
  ```

+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  @mimowo @mwielgus wdyt?
  I thought that spec defines the desired state so it's actually better fit for this field.
  But I admit I didn't think of that

```

  I'm ok either way. 
  
  Indeed, generally, controllers should modify status rather than spec. 
  
  However, Workload API is special, because it is "internal to Kueue". Note that `kueue-controller-manager` creates the Workload instance, and so it needs permissions to write spec anyway.
  
  I think conceptually, spec makes a bit more sense. Similarly as nominatedNodeName is inside Pod's spec.

+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
```

  updated

### Review by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) (commented) — 2025-06-27T18:42:55Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:343** by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) — 2025-06-27T18:42:55Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,76 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
```

  yes, I have chosen alphabetical order, I think it's good as any other, the improvement comes from the incremental addition

### Review by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) (commented) — 2025-06-27T18:44:38Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:359** by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) — 2025-06-27T18:44:38Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,76 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
```

  removed

+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.

+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.

+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.

+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  I can stick to status as initially was done - to not break the convention

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-06-27T19:09:49Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:345** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-06-27T19:07:58Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +328,70 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### Since Kueue 0.13: MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+In order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3) we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field in the Workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
```

  ```suggestion
    If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins, 
    and 3 additional clusters are nominated, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
  ```
  to make it a bit shorter while conveying the same info

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:349** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-06-27T19:08:13Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +328,70 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### Since Kueue 0.13: MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+In order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3) we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field in the Workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once.
+
+* **External**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
```

  ```suggestion
    In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is delegated to an external controller. 
  ```

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:357** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-06-27T19:09:44Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +328,70 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### Since Kueue 0.13: MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+In order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3) we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field in the Workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once.
+
+* **External**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is immutable. 
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
```

  Drop it as it is the same content as the paragraph below.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-06-27T19:24:10Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:373** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-06-27T19:24:09Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,76 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  Ah, I see, if it is going to complicate checking the "Admitted" condition to verify mutability, then I'm ok to move it to `status` actually. In any case "Workload" is API which is not facing users, only knowledgable admins, so I think we can have some freedom here.

+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+Since Kueue 0.13, in order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3), we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
+
+When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
+specified in the Workload's .spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters field.
+
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
```

  ```suggestion
  Clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
  ```

+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API

+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters

+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.

+In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field in the Workload.
+If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins, 
+and 3 additional clusters are nominated, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.

+While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is immutable. 
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+
+While the Workload is pending, the dispatcher can add or remove clusters from the list, and the Workload
+Controller synchronizes the value of the field with the subset of worker clusters with the Workload copy.

```

    // +listType=set
    // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=10
    // +optional
  ```
  It does not make sense to nominate more than the max number of clusters which is currently 10. We can revisit this in the future, but should move both at the same time.

+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.

+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:
