+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  the other way around, putting it in the `spec` make it easier thanks to validation rules

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-06-27T19:51:41Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:338** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-06-27T19:51:40Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +328,75 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+Since Kueue 0.13, in order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3), we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
+specified in the Workload's .spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters field.
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
```

  ```suggestion
  
  Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
  ```
  nit, let's make a paragraph break to separate the thoughts.

### Review by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) (commented) — 2025-07-03T14:43:21Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:373** by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2025-07-03T14:43:20Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,76 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  I am revisiting this one a bit.
  let me think this one more.

+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  ```suggestion
    nominatedClusterNames []string `json:"nominatedClusterNames,omitempty"`
  ```
  
  ```go
  type WorkloadStatus struct {
    // +optional
    clusterName *string `json:"clusterName,omitempty"`
  }
  ```
  
  After some consideration, I would propose the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` and `.status.clusterName` in the Workload API in the following reasons:
  
  Q1: Why "name" suffix?
  A1: Those fields accommodate the cluster name(s), which means those do not have any parameter for cluster identifiers, and that is exactly the cluster "name".
  
  Q2: Why not "MultiKueue" prefix?
  A2: The "Cluster" concept can be identified with exactly one semantic. The "MultiKueue" prefix is a bit redundant. Even if we introduce cluster-specific features instead of MultiKueue in the future, the Workload should have only one selected clusters field, regardless of MultiKueue, because the scheduled cluster should be selected by one field.
  
  Q3: Why not "nominatedClusterNames" in the status field?
  A3: This is indeed the desired state, and the desired field should be in the spec field. Additionally, this field is similar to nodeSelector in Pod spec rather than NNN in Pod spec because the NNN is just respected, which means the NNN might not be selected for the Pod. However, nodeSelector is always considered when the Pod is scheduled, which is the collection to select exactly one scheduling Node. 
  
  The different point across nodeSelector and nominatedClusterName is how flexible the field allows the scheduler (kube-scheduler and multikueue-dispatcher). In the nodeSelector case, the kube-scheduler is allowed to select nodes by scheduler algorithm, as long as the selected node matches the nodeSelector. In the nominatedClusterName case, it allows the multikueue-dispatcher to select a cluster only by nominated clusters, which is not allowed by multikueue-dispatcher algorithms.
  
  So, the nodeSelector in Pod can be considered as a soft restriction rather than the nominatedClusterName in Workload.
  
  Q4: Why add ".status.clusterName" to the Workload?
  A4: The current proposed ".spec.muliKueueNominatedNode" has some problems with mixed responsibilities.
  For example, the case where the Workload has QuotaReserved. In that situation, the external dispatcher might still try to replace the nominated cluster name. For sure, we can make the field immutable when the Workload has QuotaReserved. But I think we should obviously represent the fact that this Workload has already been assigned to a cluster with the assigned cluster name to avoid complex criteria for the immutable nominated cluster name.
  
  Q5: Why is "clusterName" in the status as opposed to spec, like Pod "nodeName"?
  A5: The "clusterName" is the actual state rather than the desired state. The reason why it is not in spec the same as .spec.nodeName in Pod is that the Pod nodeName is located in the spec for historical reasons. The big one of historical reasons is that the status was considered as information that could be restored from other fields when the nodeName was introduced. However, the current status field responsibility is not.
  So, the assigned cluster name must be in the status field.

  > My only small hesitation is that it is not strictly required for the feature as it would be for external automation only. Currently the selected cluster name is placed in the admission check message. It should be simple to implement so it does not seem to increase the risk much for 0.13.
  
  I believe that introducing ".status.clusterName" would be better for this feature to mitigate the edge cases for the timing when the .spec.nominatedClusterNames must be immutable.
  
  The ".status.clusterName" allows us to make the ".spec.nominatedClusterName" immutable when the ".status.clusterName" is assigned. Especially, when there are multiple AdmissionChecks, the external component can recognize whether or not it must re-assign new nominated clusters to the Workload. Otherwise, the external dispatcher needs to check the corresponding AdmissionCheck checkState and Workload QuotaReserved condition.

 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+Since Kueue 0.13, in order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3), we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
+specified in the Workload's .spec.nominatedClusterNames field.
+
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+Clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field in the Workload.
+If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins, 
+and 3 additional clusters are nominated, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once.
+
+* **External**:  
+The selection of worker clusters is delegated to an external controller. 
+The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is immutable. 
```

  ```suggestion
  While the workload `.status.clusterName` is assigned, the `nominatedClusterNames` field is immutable. 
  ```

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:385** by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2025-07-10T15:16:29Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +328,81 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+Since Kueue 0.13, in order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3), we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
+specified in the Workload's .spec.nominatedClusterNames field.
+
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+Clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field in the Workload.
+If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins, 
+and 3 additional clusters are nominated, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once.
+
+* **External**:  
+The selection of worker clusters is delegated to an external controller. 
+The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is immutable. 
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+
+While the Workload is pending, the dispatcher can add or remove clusters from the list, and the Workload
+Controller synchronizes the value of the field with the subset of worker clusters with the Workload copy.
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // nominatedClusterNames specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +listType=set
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=10
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.clusterName != null) || oldObject.spec.nominatedClusterNames == self.spec.nominatedClusterNames",message="nominatedClusterNames is immutable when the workload is assigned to a cluster"
+  // +optional
+  nominatedClusterNames []string `json:"nominatedClusterNames,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type WorkloadStatus struct {
+  // clusterName is the name of the cluster where the workload is actually assigned.
+  // +optional
+  clusterName *string `json:"clusterName,omitempty"`
+}
+```
+
+Extension of MultiKueue configuration:
+```go
+ type MultiKueue struct {
```

  ```suggestion
   type MultiKueueConfigSpec struct {
  ```
  
  Do you mean `MultiKueueConfigSpec`?

```

  ```suggestion
    // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="self.status.clusterName == null || oldObject.spec.nominatedClusterNames == self.spec.nominatedClusterNames",message="nominatedClusterNames is immutable when the workload is assigned to a cluster"
  ```
  
  Why not this one?

### Review by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) (commented) — 2025-07-10T16:41:49Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:371** by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2025-07-10T16:41:48Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +328,81 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+Since Kueue 0.13, in order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3), we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
+specified in the Workload's .spec.nominatedClusterNames field.
+
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+Clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field in the Workload.
+If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins, 
+and 3 additional clusters are nominated, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once.
+
+* **External**:  
+The selection of worker clusters is delegated to an external controller. 
+The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is immutable. 
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+
+While the Workload is pending, the dispatcher can add or remove clusters from the list, and the Workload
+Controller synchronizes the value of the field with the subset of worker clusters with the Workload copy.
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // nominatedClusterNames specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +listType=set
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=10
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.clusterName != null) || oldObject.spec.nominatedClusterNames == self.spec.nominatedClusterNames",message="nominatedClusterNames is immutable when the workload is assigned to a cluster"
```

  ~~Or we might want to use `size(self.status.clusterName) == 0` to avoid distinguishing between an empty slice and null slice.~~
  
  
  NVM, this is not a slice.

+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+Since Kueue 0.13, in order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3), we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
+specified in the Workload's .spec.nominatedClusterNames field.
+

+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+Clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field in the Workload.
+If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins, 
+and 3 additional clusters are nominated, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once.
+

+The selection of worker clusters is delegated to an external controller. 
+The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.

+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.clusterName != null) || oldObject.spec.nominatedClusterNames == self.spec.nominatedClusterNames",message="nominatedClusterNames is immutable when the workload is assigned to a cluster"
+  // +optional
+  nominatedClusterNames []string `json:"nominatedClusterNames,omitempty"`
+}
+

+  // clusterName is the name of the cluster where the workload is actually assigned.
+  // +optional
+  clusterName *string `json:"clusterName,omitempty"`

### Review by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) (commented) — 2025-07-11T08:09:55Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:350** by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) — 2025-07-11T08:09:54Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +328,81 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+Since Kueue 0.13, in order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3), we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
+specified in the Workload's .spec.nominatedClusterNames field.
+
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+Clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field in the Workload.
+If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins, 
+and 3 additional clusters are nominated, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once.
```

  I think the conclusion of the Incremental is the same as AllAtOnce.
  It goes incrementally until all clusters are nominated and stays with them nominated.
  Let's say we have 9 clusters:
  1. c1,c2,c3
  2. c1...c6
  3. c1...c9
  4. keeps c1...c9 and returns "no more workers to nominate"
  
  Maybe it should be "all workers already nominated"

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-07-11T09:10:42Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:373** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-07-11T09:10:42Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,76 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  Actually, I think it might be better to put `nominatedClusterNames` into status. The reason being to be able to reset the field on eviction (along with `status.clusterName`. Since eviction and admission only manipulate status, there is no good moment to reset spec field currently (unless we do 2 or 3-request operation).
  
  I think resetting the field on eviction is important, otherwise on re-admission the controller may see all clusters being nominated from the previous attempt.
  
  I also think the analogy with NNN may not be perfect, because Pods are never reused, contrary to Workloads in Kueue. If the Workload was single use, then we wouldn't have a need to reset the field. wdyt @tenzen-y @mszadkow ?

### Review by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) (commented) — 2025-07-11T11:22:18Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:373** by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) — 2025-07-11T11:22:18Z

@@ -316,6 +323,76 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.

+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+

+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.

+
+#### Workload Synchronization

+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  Resetting the field on the eviction is important, yes... 
  I also don't see a "proper" moment to reset this.
  
  When you think of `nominatedClusterNames` as a process of nomination rather desired state it makes sense to move it to the status.
  Bc, you can nominate let's say 5 clusters, while only one of them will become real worker (I am talking about External), so it's not desired state.
  It makes sense to have them both in status: ".status.clusterName" and ".status. nominatedClusterNames"

### Review by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) (commented) — 2025-07-11T11:37:47Z

+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  As I described in the above, the nominatedClusterNames could be considered as an along side of Pod nodeSelectors. The differences between nodeSelectors and nominatedClusterNames is flexibilities, which means the nominiatedClusterName is more fixed.
  
  The NNN and nominatedClusterName is similar name, but functionality is completely difference since nominatedClusterName must be respected, but NNN might be respected which means the kube-scheduler might assign Node to Pod even if the node does not match NNN field.
  
  I think we do not need to reset nominatedClusterName when the Workload is evicted, which is similar concept of mutable scheduling directives (nodeSelector, etc.) for suspended Jobs.
  
  Even if the Job is suspended, the nodeSelectors are not reset.

### Review by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) (commented) — 2025-07-11T11:38:42Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:385** by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2025-07-11T11:38:42Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +328,81 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+Since Kueue 0.13, in order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3), we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
+specified in the Workload's .spec.nominatedClusterNames field.
+
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+Clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field in the Workload.
+If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins, 
+and 3 additional clusters are nominated, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once.
+
+* **External**:  
+The selection of worker clusters is delegated to an external controller. 
+The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is immutable. 
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+
+While the Workload is pending, the dispatcher can add or remove clusters from the list, and the Workload
+Controller synchronizes the value of the field with the subset of worker clusters with the Workload copy.
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // nominatedClusterNames specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +listType=set
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=10
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.clusterName != null) || oldObject.spec.nominatedClusterNames == self.spec.nominatedClusterNames",message="nominatedClusterNames is immutable when the workload is assigned to a cluster"
+  // +optional
+  nominatedClusterNames []string `json:"nominatedClusterNames,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type WorkloadStatus struct {
+  // clusterName is the name of the cluster where the workload is actually assigned.
+  // +optional
+  clusterName *string `json:"clusterName,omitempty"`
+}
+```
+
+Extension of MultiKueue configuration:
+```go
+ type MultiKueue struct {
```

  I see. In that case, could you mention that?

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-07-11T11:43:54Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:373** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-07-11T11:43:54Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,76 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  I think there is some misunderstanding here. 
  
  I think actually reseting the clusters is quite important, otherwise after re-admission we will start to admit into all clusters again at the same time. Maybe for some use cases we could have a knob to keep them, but I think the baseline functionality should reset, thus some analogy may not be perfect.
  
  Regarding nodeSelectors they are actually reset on eviction, so that we can set new node selectors if we admit to another ResourceFlavor

+The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field in the Workload.
+If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins, 
+and 3 additional clusters are nominated, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once.
```

  IIUC they do not get rejected, they stay nominated for admission from point of view of this feature.
  Do you want to set the rejection state after another round has expired?

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-07-11T16:38:04Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:350** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-07-11T16:38:04Z

@@ -316,6 +328,81 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+Since Kueue 0.13, in order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3), we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
+specified in the Workload's .spec.nominatedClusterNames field.
+
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+Clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field in the Workload.
+If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins, 
+and 3 additional clusters are nominated, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once.
```

  Good question. I think this would be a sensible extension, but I wouldnt say it is necessary in first iteration. Note that we dont reject the workload until 0.12 with the built in dispatcher.

+When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
+specified in the Workload's .spec.nominatedClusterNames field.
+
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+Clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field in the Workload.
+If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins,

### Review by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) (commented) — 2025-07-11T17:27:26Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:373** by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2025-07-11T17:27:26Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,76 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  I still think that the nominatedClusterNames would be spec since it is just candidates, which is not actual state.
  In the case of Ingress loadBalancer field, those are the actual state which is assigned IP, ports, and hostName.

### Review by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) (commented) — 2025-07-11T17:31:56Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:385** by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) — 2025-07-11T17:31:56Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +328,81 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+Since Kueue 0.13, in order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3), we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
+specified in the Workload's .spec.nominatedClusterNames field.
+
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+Clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field in the Workload.
+If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins, 
+and 3 additional clusters are nominated, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once.
+
+* **External**:  
+The selection of worker clusters is delegated to an external controller. 
+The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is immutable. 
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+
+While the Workload is pending, the dispatcher can add or remove clusters from the list, and the Workload
+Controller synchronizes the value of the field with the subset of worker clusters with the Workload copy.
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // nominatedClusterNames specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +listType=set
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:MaxItems=10
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.clusterName != null) || oldObject.spec.nominatedClusterNames == self.spec.nominatedClusterNames",message="nominatedClusterNames is immutable when the workload is assigned to a cluster"
+  // +optional
+  nominatedClusterNames []string `json:"nominatedClusterNames,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type WorkloadStatus struct {
+  // clusterName is the name of the cluster where the workload is actually assigned.
+  // +optional
+  clusterName *string `json:"clusterName,omitempty"`
+}
+```
+
+Extension of MultiKueue configuration:
+```go
+ type MultiKueue struct {
```

  As mentioned in https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/5410#discussion_r2200829408
  More specific comment was added

+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  Well I would argue it describes the current state of the nomination set. They are real in the sense that Kueue performs traffic to the clusters. Similarly as traffic is performed based on the loadBalancer IPs.
  
  Pragmatically also keeping the field in spec means two downsides:
  1.This means extra qps to reset
  2. the reset is no longer atomic so it requires to design when and how to clear the field to avoid race conditions. For example, if we just clear while evicted it may get re admitted before we clear. 
  
  iirc similar considerations lead us in the past to move Admission under .status.admission, even though in Alpha API of Kueue it was in spec.

+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  @tenzen-y, I consider the Workload API it is for admins and automation, so I would prefer to make pragmatic choices about it.  If we put it into spec, then we need to design how the flow of eviction and re-admission will look like.
  
  Are there any downsides of putting the field into status, which could bite us in the foreseeable future?

+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  I would approve `.status.nominatedClusterNames`.
  As an additional request, I would like to reset the nominatedClusterNames (NCNs) when the Workload gets .status.clusterName. In other words, I would like to add a Workload validation so that Workload does not have both clusterName and NCNs, which means both fields are mutually exclusive. However, the resetting of the NCNs field is responsible for the dispatcher even when a specified dispatcher is external.
  
  ---
  After more consideration, I could find that there is no way to guarantee the atomic behavior when the dispatcher needs to reset the NCNs as you mentioned. 
  
  However, in the case of external dispatchers, the race condition issue still could occur because the updating of Admission state is out of the scope of external dispatchers. In other words, when they use an external dispatcher, we still need 2 API requests by the kueue-controller-manager and an external dispatcher. 
  
  This KEP aims to implement and expose the dispatching mechanism. So, I think we could revisit in the next iteration how to mitigate the non atomic behavior when they use an external dispatcher.

  > However, in the case of external dispatchers, the race condition issue still could occur because the updating of Admission state is out of the scope of external dispatchers. In other words, when they use an external dispatcher, we still need 2 API requests by the kueue-controller-manager and an external dispatcher.
  
  I expect the external dispatcher, when giving up, to set the Workloads status.admissionCheck.state to Retry. This will trigger the internal Workload controller to Evict the workload and as part of the evictions to reset the status.nominatedClusterNames field, along with resetting status.clusterName.
  
  So I dont see any race condition for external dispatchers in this model.

```

  Alternatively, maybe the easier approach would be to update `status.nominatedClusterNames` to just match the `status.clusterName`, when `status.clusterName` is set.
  
  Let me also summarize the actors operating on the fields:
  -  `status.nominatedClusterNames` - manipulated by an external controller (dispatcher), only reset on eviction by the Workload MK controller
  - `status.clusterName` - only set by the Workload MK controller.
  
  Since  `status.clusterName` is only set by the Workload MK controller, then  `status.nominatedClusterNames`  could also be manipulated by it. So we have 3 options when setting `status.clusterName` :
  1. reset   `status.nominatedClusterNames`  to nil, but then we cannot validate `status.clusterName` was nominated in webhooks
  2. set `status.nominatedClusterNames` also to  `status.clusterName` 
  3. don't update `status.nominatedClusterNames`, use it to validate in webhooks, but then document it is ignored
  
  I would be leaning to (2.) as allows to validate, and we don't really need to say it is ignored, it is just updated to match clusterName. wdyt @tenzen-y ?

+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  > > I would like to add a Workload validation so that Workload does not have both clusterName and NCNs, which means both fields are mutually exclusive. However, the resetting of the NCNs field is responsible for the dispatcher even when a specified dispatcher is external.
  > 
  > As we discussed with Marcin we would like to validate so that the selected cluster is.among the set of nominated clusters, to prevent races when external dispatcher removes NCN selected by MK WorkloadController concurrently. However, if we clear NCN this becomes tricker. We could also clear NCN in a follow up request, but this means extra qps.
  > 
  > So I was thinking about just saying that whenever clusterName is set it is validated against NCN, and at that point NCN is ignored. wdyt?
  
  I think both nominatedClusterNames and clusterName must not exist together. If we allow that, we should move the nominatedClsuterNames to spec since in the case of allowing coexistence those, the NCNs is no longer current state.
  
  Additionally, I don't think the race is problem since the race could be resolved by external dispatcher reconciliation mechanism. When they face updating NCNs error, the dispatcher reconciler just requeue it to workqueue by error. And then in the next reconciliation, it checks if the clusterName already has been selected. After the external dispatcher recognizes the selected clusterName, it just ignore NCNs updating.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-07-17T05:43:13Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:373** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-07-17T05:43:13Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +323,76 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+The MultiKueue Workload Controller consists of nomination nd synchronization: 
+first, it nominates worker clusters for each workload based on the configured dispatching mode;
+then, it synchronizes the workload by creating and managing its copies in the nominated clusters. 
+This ensures that only one cluster ultimately admits and runs the workload, 
+while the management cluster maintains up-to-date status by tracking the admitted job.
+
+#### Cluster Nomination
+Cluster nomination phase looks differently depending on the configured dispatching mode.
+MultiKueue supports three dispatching modes: AllAtOnce (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-all-at-once`),
+Incremental (`kueue.x-k8s.io/multikueue-dispatcher-incremental`), and External.
+
+* **AllAtOnce Mode**:  
+  In this mode, all available clusters are considered for dispatching at once, and the workload is copied to each worker cluster.
+
+* **Incremental Mode**:  
+  In this mode, clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+  The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are added to the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field.
+  During the first 5-minute round, only these clusters are eligible to admit the workload.
+  If none of the initial clusters admit the workload within the round's duration, the next round begins, and 3 additional clusters are nominated.
+  This incremental approach continues, adding 3 more clusters in each subsequent round, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+  This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once,
+  which can help optimize resource usage and reduce unnecessary workload duplication.
+
+* **External Mode**:  
+  In this mode, the selection of worker clusters is entirely delegated to an external controller. 
+  The external controller is responsible for setting the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+  If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+  While the workload is in the admitted state, the `MultiKueueNominatedClusters` field is treated as immutable. 
+  Any updates to this field while the workload is admitted will be rejected by the MultiKueue controller 
+  to ensure scheduling consistency and prevent unintended cluster transitions.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+Based on the `.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters` field, the actual copy of the workload is created in
+the nominated worker clusters. The MultiKueue Workload Controller ensures that the workload is
+synchronized from the management cluster to the selected worker clusters.
+
+Once the workload is admitted and other clusters are cleaned up, the real job is created to match the
+workload. This guarantees that the workload will not start in more than one cluster. The workload will
+also receive an annotation indicating the cluster where it is actually running.
+
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadSpec struct {
+  // MultiKueueNominatedClusters specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling by MultiKueue.
+  // This field is optional.
+  // 
+  // +optional
+  // +kubebuilder:validation:XValidation:rule="!(self.status.conditions.exists(c, c.type == 'Admitted')) || oldObject.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters == self.spec.multiKueueNominatedClusters",message="multiKueueNominatedClusters is immutable when the workload is in the 'Admitted' state"
+  // This field is immutable while the workload is admitted. Any attempt to modify it during the admitted state will be rejected by the controller.
+  MultiKueueNominatedClusters []string `json:"multiKueueNominatedClusters,omitempty"`
```

  > I think both nominatedClusterNames and clusterName must not exist together. If we allow that, we should move the nominatedClsuterNames to spec since in the case of allowing coexistence those, the NCNs is no longer current state.
  
  My only concern was about validation here, but actually the webhook could compare the old version of nominatedClusterNames when new clusterName is set. So I'm good with that. I think this will work fine.
  
  
  > Additionally, I don't think the race is problem since the race could be resolved by external dispatcher reconciliation mechanism. When they face updating NCNs error, the dispatcher reconciler just requeue it to workqueue by error. And then in the next reconciliation, it checks if the clusterName already has been selected. After the external dispatcher recognizes the selected clusterName, it just ignore NCNs updating.
  
  Yeah, I think this is not an issue.

### Review by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) (commented) — 2025-07-17T05:53:54Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:350** by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2025-07-17T05:53:54Z
```diff
@@ -316,6 +328,81 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+Since Kueue 0.13, in order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3), we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
+specified in the Workload's .spec.nominatedClusterNames field.
+
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation. 
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+Clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.spec.nominatedClusterNames` field in the Workload.
+If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins, 
+and 3 additional clusters are nominated, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once.
```

  This could be resolved.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2025-07-17T06:47:36Z

```diff
@@ -316,6 +328,80 @@ that ware created by this multikueue manager cluster and delete them if their lo
 - `WorkerLostTimeout` - defines the time a local workload's multikueue admission check state is kept Ready
 if the connection with its reserving worker cluster is lost.
 
+
+### MultiKueue Dispatcher API
+
+Since Kueue 0.13, in order to meet the requirements of [Story 3](#story-3), we introduce an API for custom dispatching algorithms.
+When a custom Dispatcher API is used, instead of creating the copy of the Workload on all clusters the
+the MultiKueue Workload Controller only creates the copy of the Workload on the subset of worker clusters
+specified in the Workload's .status.nominatedClusterNames field.
+
+Additionally, we implement a built-in incremental dispatcher as a reference implementation.
+Including the pre-existing dispatching algorithm until 0.12, we distinguish the following dispatchers:
+
+* **AllAtOnce**:  
+The workload is copied to all available worker clusters at once. This is the default dispatching algorithm.
+
+* **Incremental**:  
+Clusters are nominated incrementally in rounds of fixed duration (5 minutes per round). 
+The process begins by nominating an initial set of 3 clusters, which are set in the `.status.nominatedClusterNames` field in the Workload.
+If none of the clusters admit the workload within the current round's duration, the next round begins, 
+and 3 additional clusters are nominated, until the workload is admitted or all eligible clusters have been considered.
+This strategy allows for a controlled and gradual expansion of candidate clusters, rather than dispatching the workload to all clusters at once.
+
+* **External**:  
+The selection of worker clusters is delegated to an external controller. 
+The external controller is responsible for setting the `.status.nominatedClusterNames` field to the names of the selected clusters.
+If the nominated clusters field is changed by the external controller, workloads are removed from any clusters that are no longer nominated.
+While the workload `.status.clusterName` is assigned, the `nominatedClusterNames` field is immutable.
+
+#### Workload Synchronization
+
+While the Workload is pending, the dispatcher can add or remove clusters from the list, and the Workload
+Controller synchronizes the value of the field with the subset of worker clusters with the Workload copy.
+
+Changes to Workload type:
+```go
+type WorkloadStatus struct {
+  // nominatedClusterNames specifies the list of cluster names that have been nominated for scheduling.
+  // While the workload `.status.clusterName` is assigned, the field is immutable.
```

  ```suggestion
    // This field is mutually exclusive with the `.status.clusterName` field, and is reset when 
    // `status.clusterName` is set.
  ```
  It implies the field is immutable while  `status.clusterName` is set.
